## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. In chemical kinetics, rate laws relate reaction rates to concentrations via power-law, rational, or more complex functional forms depending on the reaction mechanism.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with constant product)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction with competitive adsorption)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-dependent rate constant)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple simultaneous pathways)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with background rate)
- Time-modulated rate: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (linearly changing rate constant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate values (consumption) with magnitude increasing with concentration â†’ negative power-law: dA_dt = -c * A**n with c > 0
- Rate approaching zero as A approaches zero with finite slope â†’ first-order kinetics dominates at low concentrations
- Rate leveling off at high concentration â†’ saturation mechanism suggesting rational function A/(c + A)
- Rate passing through a maximum then decreasing â†’ substrate inhibition or autocatalytic mechanism with depletion term
- Rate depending on (c - A) terms â†’ indicates approach to equilibrium or conservation constraint from stoichiometry
- Concentration-independent residual rate at low A â†’ zero-order contribution suggesting catalytic or externally driven process
- Rate changing sign at specific A value â†’ reversible reaction with equilibrium concentration at the sign change
- Explicit time dependence in rate â†’ catalyst deactivation, photochemical initiation, or temperature ramping effects
- Quadratic dependence on A at low concentrations transitioning to linear at high â†’ bimolecular mechanism with one reactant in excess
- Product of A and (1-A/c) type structure â†’ conservation law constraining total concentration in closed system
